</p><p>Gender discrimination also helps explain the differences between trial outcomes in which some female defendants are sentenced to death and other female defendants are sentenced to lesser punishments. <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Barron" title="Phillip Barron">Phillip Barron</a> argues that female defendants are more likely to be sentenced to death for crimes that violate gender norms, such as killing children or killing strangers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup>
</p><p>Transgender people face widespread discrimination while incarcerated. They are generally housed according to their legal birth sex, rather than their gender identity. Studies have shown that transgender people are at an increased risk for harassment and sexual assault in this environment. They may also be denied access to medical procedures related to their reassignment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some countries use <a href="/wiki/Stoning" title="Stoning">stoning</a> as a form of capital punishment. According to Amnesty International, the majority of those stoned are women and women are disproportionately affected by stoning because of sexism in the legal system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup>
</p><p>
One study found that: </p><blockquote><p>[O]n average, women receive lighter sentences in comparison with men<span class="nowrap"> </span>... roughly 30% of the gender differences in incarceration cannot be explained by the observed criminal characteristics of offense and offender. We also find evidence of considerable heterogeneity across judges in their treatment of female and male offenders. There is little evidence, however, that tastes for gender discrimination are driving the mean gender disparity or the variance in treatment between judges.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>A 2017 study by Knepper found that "female plaintiffs filing workplace sex discrimination claims are substantially more likely to settle and win compensation whenever a female judge is assigned to the case. Additionally, female judges are 15 percentage points less likely than male judges to grant motions filed by defendants, which suggests that final negotiations are shaped by the emergence of the bias."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sex_differences_in_education" title="Sex differences in education">Sex differences in education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sexism_in_academia" title="Sexism in academia">Sexism in academia</a></div>
<p>Women have traditionally had limited access to higher education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (April 2018)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the past, when women were admitted to higher education, they were encouraged to major in less-scientific subjects; the study of <a href="/wiki/English_literature" title="English literature">English literature</a> in American and British colleges and universities was instituted as a field considered suitable to women's "lesser intellects".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (April 2018)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Educational specialties in higher education produce and perpetuate inequality between men and women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> Disparity persists particularly in computer and <a href="/wiki/Information_science" title="Information science">information science</a>, where in the US women received only 21% of the undergraduate degrees, and in engineering, where women obtained only 19% of the degrees in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> Only one out of five of physics doctorates in the US are awarded to women, and only about half those women are American.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physics_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-physics-295">[295]</a></sup> Of all the physics professors in the country, only 14% are women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physics_295-1"><a href="#cite_note-physics-295">[295]</a></sup> As of 2019, women account for just 27% of all workers in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/STEM" title="STEM">STEM</a> fields, and on average earn almost 20% less than men in the same industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup>
</p><p>World <a href="/wiki/Literacy#Gender_disparities" title="Literacy">literacy</a> is lower for females than for males. Data from <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a></i> shows that 79.7% of women are literate, compared to 88.6% of men (aged 15 and over).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> In some parts of the world, girls continue to be excluded from proper public or private education. In parts of Afghanistan, girls who go to school face serious violence from some local community members and religious groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edition.cnn.com_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-edition.cnn.com-298">[298]</a></sup> According to 2010 UN estimates, only Afghanistan, Pakistan and Yemen had less than 90 girls per 100 boys at school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> Jayachandran and <a href="/wiki/Adriana_Lleras-Muney" title="Adriana Lleras-Muney">Lleras-Muney's</a> study of Sri Lankan economic development has suggested that increases in the life expectancy for women encourages educational investment because a longer time horizon increases the value of investments that pay out over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup>
</p><p>Educational opportunities and outcomes for women have greatly improved in the West. Since 1991, the proportion of women enrolled in college in the United States has exceeded the enrollment rate for men, and the gap has widened over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sexism&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, women made up the majority—54%—of the 10.8 million college students enrolled in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> However, research by Diane Halpern has indicated that boys receive more attention, praise, blame and punishment in the grammar-school classroom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> and "this pattern of more active teacher attention directed at male students continues at the postsecondary level".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> Over time, female students speak less in a classroom setting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> Teachers also tend to spend more time supporting the academic achievements of girls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup>
</p><p>Boys are frequently diagnosed with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ADHD" title="ADHD">ADHD</a>, which some see as a result of school systems being more likely to apply these labels to males.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> A recent study by the OECD in over 60 countries found that teachers give boys lower grades for the same work. The researchers attribute this to stereotypical ideas about boys and recommend teachers to be aware of this gender bias.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup> One study found that students give female professors worse evaluation scores than male professors, even though the students appear to do as well under female professors as male professors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup>
</p><p>Gender bias and gender-based discrimination still permeate the education process in many settings. For example, in the teaching and learning process, including differential engagement, expectations and interactions by <a href="/wiki/Teacher" title="Teacher">teachers</a> with their male and female students, as well as gender stereotypes in <a href="/wiki/Textbook" title="Textbook">textbooks</a> and learning materials. There has been a lack in adequate resources and infrastructure to ensure safe and enabling <a href="/wiki/Learning_environment" title="Learning environment">learning environments</a>, and insufficient <a href="/wiki/Policy" title="Policy">policy</a>, legal and planning frameworks, that respect, protect and fulfil the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_education" title="Right to education">right to education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Foot_binding" title="Foot binding">Foot binding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burqa" title="Burqa">Burqa</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Gendered_associations_of_pink_and_blue" title="Gendered associations of pink and blue">Gendered associations of pink and blue</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gobert_-_Louis_XV_as_child,_Fundaci%C3%B3n_Jakober.jpg"><img alt="Louis XV as a boy wearing a pink dress." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="350" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Gobert_-_Louis_XV_as_child%2C_Fundaci%C3%B3n_Jakober.jpg/170px-Gobert_-_Louis_XV_as_child%2C_Fundaci%C3%B3n_Jakober.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Gobert_-_Louis_XV_as_child%2C_Fundaci%C3%B3n_Jakober.jpg/255px-Gobert_-_Louis_XV_as_child%2C_Fundaci%C3%B3n_Jakober.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Gobert_-_Louis_XV_as_child%2C_Fundaci%C3%B3n_Jakober.jpg/340px-Gobert_-_Louis_XV_as_child%2C_Fundaci%C3%B3n_Jakober.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gobert_-_Louis_XV_as_child,_Fundaci%C3%B3n_Jakober.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Louis_XV" title="Louis XV">Louis XV</a> in 1712, a boy wearing a pink dress</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_HIGH_CASTE_LADYS_DAINTY_LILY_FEET.jpg"><img alt="A Chinese woman shows the effects of foot binding on her feet." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1968" data-file-width="1911" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/A_HIGH_CASTE_LADYS_DAINTY_LILY_FEET.jpg/170px-A_HIGH_CASTE_LADYS_DAINTY_LILY_FEET.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/A_HIGH_CASTE_LADYS_DAINTY_LILY_FEET.jpg/255px-A_HIGH_CASTE_LADYS_DAINTY_LILY_FEET.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/A_HIGH_CASTE_LADYS_DAINTY_LILY_FEET.jpg/340px-A_HIGH_CASTE_LADYS_DAINTY_LILY_FEET.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_HIGH_CASTE_LADYS_DAINTY_LILY_FEET.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chinese woman shows the effect of <a href="/wiki/Foot_binding" title="Foot binding">foot binding</a></div></div></div>
<p>Feminists argue that clothing and footwear fashion have been oppressive to women, restricting their movements, increasing their vulnerability, and endangering their health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup> Using thin models in the fashion industry has encouraged the development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulimia" title="Bulimia">bulimia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anorexia_nervosa" title="Anorexia nervosa">anorexia nervosa</a>, as well as locking female consumers into false feminine identities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup>
</p><p>The assignment of gender-specific baby clothes can instill in children a belief in negative gender stereotypes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> One example is the assignment in some countries of the color pink to girls and blue to boys. The fashion is recent one. At the beginning of the 20th century the trend was the opposite: blue for girls and pink for boys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup> In the early 1900s, <i>The Women's Journal</i> wrote that "pink being a more decided and stronger colour, is more suitable for the boy, while blue, which is more delicate and dainty, is prettier for the girl". <i>DressMaker</i> magazine also explained that "[t]he preferred colour to dress young boys in is pink. Blue is reserved for girls as it is considered paler, and the more dainty of the two colours, and pink is thought to be stronger (akin to red)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup> Today, in many countries, it is considered inappropriate for boys to wear dresses and skirts, but this is also a relatively recent view. From the mid-16th century<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> until the late 19th or early 20th century, young boys in the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a> were <a href="/wiki/Breeching_(boys)" title="Breeching (boys)">unbreeched</a> and wore <a href="/wiki/Gown" title="Gown">gowns</a> or dresses until an age that varied between two and eight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup>
</p><p>Laws that dictate how women must dress are seen by many international human rights organizations, such as Amnesty International, as gender discrimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doc.es.amnesty.org_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-doc.es.amnesty.org-318">[318]</a></sup> In many countries, women face violence for failing to adhere to certain dress codes, whether by the authorities (such as the <a href="/wiki/Religious_police" title="Religious police">religious police</a>), family members, or the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> Amnesty International states:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Interpretations of religion, culture, or tradition cannot justify imposing rules about dress on those who choose to dress differently. States should take measures to protect individuals from being coerced to dress in specific ways by family members, community or religious groups or leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doc.es.amnesty.org_318-1"><a href="#cite_note-doc.es.amnesty.org-318">[318]</a></sup>}}</p></blockquote>
<p>The production process also faces criticism for sexist practices. In the garment industry, approximately 80 percent of workers are female.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> Much garment production is located in Asia because of low labor costs. Women who work in these factories are sexually harassed by managers and male workers, paid low wages, and <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_discrimination" title="Pregnancy discrimination">discriminated against when pregnant</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conscription">Conscription</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Conscription_and_sexism" title="Conscription and sexism">Conscription and sexism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Karakal_Winter_Training_(1).jpg"><img alt="Three armed female soldiers" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1675" data-file-width="2568" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Karakal_Winter_Training_%281%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Karakal_Winter_Training_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Karakal_Winter_Training_%281%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Karakal_Winter_Training_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Karakal_Winter_Training_%281%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Karakal_Winter_Training_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Karakal_Winter_Training_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Israeli female soldiers</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">Conscription</a>, or compulsory military service, has been criticized as sexist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benatar_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-Benatar-323">[323]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 102">: 102 </span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> Prior to the late 20th century, only men were subjected to conscription,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benatar_323-1"><a href="#cite_note-Benatar-323">[323]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 255">: 255 </span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> and most countries still require only men to serve in the military.
</p><p>In his book <i>The Second Sexism: Discrimination Against Men and Boys</i> (2012), philosopher <a href="/wiki/David_Benatar" title="David Benatar">David Benatar</a> states that "[t]he prevailing assumption is that where conscription is necessary, it is only men who should be conscripted and, similarly, that only males should be forced into combat". This, he believes, "is a sexist assumption".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benatar_323-2"><a href="#cite_note-Benatar-323">[323]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 102">: 102 </span></sup> Anthropologist Ayse Gül Altinay has commented that "given equal suffrage rights, there is no other citizenship practice that differentiates as radically between men and women as compulsory male conscription".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altinay_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-Altinay-329">[329]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 34">: 34 </span></sup>
</p><p>Only nine countries conscript women into their armed forces: China, Eritrea, Israel, Libya, Malaysia, North Korea, Norway, Peru, and Taiwan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-330">[330]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norway_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norway-331">[331]</a></sup> Other countries—such as <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Finland" title="Conscription in Finland">Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Turkey" title="Conscription in Turkey">Turkey</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Singapore" title="Conscription in Singapore">Singapore</a>—still use a system of conscription which requires military service from men only, although women may serve voluntarily. In 2014, Norway became the first <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> country to introduce obligatory military service for women as an act of gender equality<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norway_331-1"><a href="#cite_note-Norway-331">[331]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> and in 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> government started preparing a gender-neutral draft law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> The gender selective draft has been challenged in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-Sexism-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Sexism_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Sexism_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">There is a clear and broad consensus among academic scholars in multiple fields that sexism refers primarily to discrimination against women, and primarily affects women. See, for example:
<ul><li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1067248974">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit;word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output .citation:target{background-color:rgba(0,127,255,0.133)}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-free a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-free a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Lock-green.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .id-lock-registration a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-registration a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d6/Lock-gray-alt-2.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-subscription a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-subscription a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/Lock-red-alt-2.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .cs1-ws-icon a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg")right 0.1em center/12px .cs1-visible-error{color:#d33}.mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{display:none;color:#3a3;margin-left:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right{padding-right:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .citation .mw-selflink{font-weight:inherit}</style><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1">"Sexism". <i>New Oxford American Dictionary</i> (3 ed.). <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>. 2010. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780199891535" title="Special:BookSources/9780199891535"><bdi>9780199891535</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=New+Oxford+American+Dictionary&amp;rft.edition=3&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=9780199891535&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Defines sexism as "prejudice, stereotyping, or discrimination, typically against women, on the basis of sex".</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1">"Sexism". <i>Encyclopædia Britannica, Online Academic Edition</i>. 2015.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica%2C+Online+Academic+Edition&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Defines sexism as "prejudice or discrimination based on sex or gender, especially against women and girls". Notes that "sexism in a society is most commonly applied against women and girls. It functions to maintain patriarchy, or male domination, through ideological and material practices of individuals, collectives, and institutions that oppress women and girls on the basis of sex or gender."</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFCuddJones2005">Cudd, Ann E.; Jones, Leslie E. (2005). "Sexism". <i>A Companion to Applied Ethics</i>. London: <a href="/wiki/Wiley-Blackwell" title="Wiley-Blackwell">Blackwell</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=A+Companion+to+Applied+Ethics&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pub=Blackwell&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.aulast=Cudd&amp;rft.aufirst=Ann+E.&amp;rft.au=Jones%2C+Leslie+E.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Notes that <span style="padding-right:.15em;">"</span>'Sexism' refers to a historically and globally pervasive form of oppression against women."</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFMasequesmay2008">Masequesmay, Gina (2008). "Sexism".  In O'Brien, Jodi (ed.). <i>Encyclopedia of Gender and Society</i>. <a href="/wiki/SAGE_Publishing" title="SAGE Publishing">SAGE Publishing</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Gender+and+Society&amp;rft.pub=SAGE+Publishing&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.aulast=Masequesmay&amp;rft.aufirst=Gina&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Notes that "sexism usually refers to prejudice or discrimination based on sex or gender, especially against women and girls". Also states that "sexism is an ideology or practices that maintain patriarchy or male domination."</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFHornsby2005">Hornsby, Jennifer (2005). "Sexism".  In Honderich, Ted (ed.). <i>The Oxford Companion to Philosophy</i> (2 ed.). Oxford University Press.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=The+Oxford+Companion+to+Philosophy&amp;rft.edition=2&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.aulast=Hornsby&amp;rft.aufirst=Jennifer&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Defines sexism as "thought or practice which may permeate language and which assumes women's inferiority to men".</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1">"Sexism". <i>Collins Dictionary of Sociology</i>. <a href="/wiki/HarperCollins" title="HarperCollins">HarperCollins</a>. 2006.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=Collins+Dictionary+of+Sociology&amp;rft.pub=HarperCollins&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Defines sexism as "any devaluation or denigration of women or men, but particularly women, which is embodied in institutions and social relationships."</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1">"Sexism". <i>Palgrave MacMillan Dictionary of Political Thought</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palgrave_MacMillan" title="Palgrave MacMillan">Palgrave MacMillan</a>. 2007.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=Palgrave+MacMillan+Dictionary+of+Political+Thought&amp;rft.pub=Palgrave+MacMillan&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Notes that "either sex may be the object of sexist attitudes<span class="nowrap"> </span>... however, it is commonly held that, in developed societies, women have been the usual victims".</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1">"Sexism". <i>The Greenwood Encyclopedia of Love, Courtship, and Sexuality through History, Volume 6: The Modern World</i>. <a href="/wiki/Greenwood_Publishing_Group" title="Greenwood Publishing Group">Greenwood</a>. 2007.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=The+Greenwood+Encyclopedia+of+Love%2C+Courtship%2C+and+Sexuality+through+History%2C+Volume+6%3A+The+Modern+World&amp;rft.pub=Greenwood&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> "Sexism is any act, attitude, or institutional configuration that systematically subordinates or devalues women. Built upon the belief that men and women are constitutionally different, sexism takes these differences as indications that men are inherently superior to women, which then is used to justify the nearly universal dominance of men in social and familial relationships, as well as politics, religion, language, law, and economics."</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFFoster2011">Foster, Carly Hayden (2011). "Sexism".  In Kurlan, George Thomas (ed.). <i>The Encyclopedia of Political Science</i>. <a href="/wiki/CQ_Press" title="CQ Press">CQ Press</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781608712434" title="Special:BookSources/9781608712434"><bdi>9781608712434</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=The+Encyclopedia+of+Political+Science&amp;rft.pub=CQ+Press&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.isbn=9781608712434&amp;rft.aulast=Foster&amp;rft.aufirst=Carly+Hayden&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Notes that "both men and women can experience sexism, but sexism against women is more pervasive".</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFJohnson2000">Johnson, Allan G. (2000). "Sexism". <i>The Blackwell Dictionary of Sociology</i>. Blackwell.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sexism&amp;rft.btitle=The+Blackwell+Dictionary+of+Sociology&amp;rft.pub=Blackwell&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.aulast=Johnson&amp;rft.aufirst=Allan+G.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Suggests that "the key test of whether something is sexist<span class="nowrap"> </span>... lies in its consequences: if it supports male privilege, then it is by definition sexist. I specify 'male privilege' because in every known society where gender inequality exists, males are privileged over females."</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLorber2011">Lorber, Judith (2011). <i>Gender Inequality: Feminist Theories and Politics</i>. Oxford University Press. p. 5.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Gender+Inequality%3A+Feminist+Theories+and+Politics&amp;rft.pages=5&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.aulast=Lorber&amp;rft.aufirst=Judith&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> Notes that "although we speak of gender inequality, it is usually women who are disadvantaged relative to similarly situated men".</li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFWortmanLoftusWeaver1999">Wortman, Camille B.; Loftus, Elizabeth S.; Weaver, Charles A (1999). <i>Psychology</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McGraw-Hill" title="McGraw-Hill">McGraw-Hill</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Psychology&amp;rft.pub=McGraw-Hill&amp;rft.date=1999&amp;rft.aulast=Wortman&amp;rft.aufirst=Camille+B.&amp;rft.au=Loftus%2C+Elizabeth+S.&amp;rft.au=Weaver%2C+Charles+A&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span> "As throughout history, today women are the primary victims of sexism, prejudice directed at one sex, even in the United States."</li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFMatsumoto2001">Matsumoto, David (2001). <i>The Handbook of Culture and Psychology</i>. <li id="cite_note-Macklem-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Macklem_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Macklem_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFMacklem2003">Macklem, Tony (2003). <i>Beyond Comparison: Sex and Discrimination</i>. New York: <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Press" title="Cambridge University Press">Cambridge University Press</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-82682-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-82682-2"><bdi>978-0-521-82682-2</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Beyond+Comparison%3A+Sex+and+Discrimination&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-82682-2&amp;rft.aulast=Macklem&amp;rft.aufirst=Tony&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Lenhart-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Lenhart_7-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Lenhart_7-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Lenhart_7-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFSharyn_Ann_Lenhart2004">Sharyn Ann Lenhart (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Rt2SAgAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA6" rel="nofollow"><i>Clinical Aspects of Sexual Harassment and Gender Discrimination: Psychological Consequences and Treatment Interventions</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>. p. 6. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1135941314" title="Special:BookSources/978-1135941314"><bdi>978-1135941314</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">April 20,</span> 2018</span>. <q>Gender or Sex Discrimination: This term refers to the types of gender bias that have a negative impact. The term has legal, as well as theoretical and psychological, definitions. Psychological consequences can be more readily inferred from the latter, but both definitions are of significance. Theoretically, gender discrimination has been described as (1) the unequal rewards that men and women receive in the workplace or academic environment because of their gender or sex difference (DiThomaso, 1989); (2) a process occurring in work or educational settings in which an individual is overtly or covertly limited access to an opportunity or a resource because of a sex or is given the opportunity or the resource reluctantly and may face harassment for picking it (Roeske &amp; Pleck, 1983); or (3) both.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Clinical+Aspects+of+Sexual+Harassment+and+Gender+Discrimination%3A+Psychological+Consequences+and+Treatment+Interventions&amp;rft.pages=6&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-1135941314&amp;rft.au=Sharyn+Ann+Lenhart&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DRt2SAgAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA6&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-178"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-178">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://definitions.uslegal.com/p/prostitution" rel="nofollow">"Prostitution Law &amp; Legal Definition"</a>. US Legal<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">March 19,</span> 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Prostitution+Law+%26+Legal+Definition&amp;rft.pub=US+Legal&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fdefinitions.uslegal.com%2Fp%2Fprostitution&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-sullivan-179"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-sullivan_179-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-sullivan_179-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSullivan,_Barbara2007">Sullivan, Barbara (2007). "Rape, Prostitution and Consent". <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Australian_and_New_Zealand_Journal_of_Criminology" title="The Australian and New Zealand Journal of Criminology">The Australian and New Zealand Journal of Criminology</a></i>. <b>40</b> (2): 127–142. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1375%2Facri.40.2.127" rel="nofollow">10.1375/acri.40.2.127</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:145263451" rel="nofollow">145263451</a>. <q>In common law jurisdictions like the United Kingdom, Australia, New Zealand and Canada, some of the evidentiary jurisprudence clearly linked chastity with veracity. So women who were or had been sex workers, those who were 'rumoured' to be prostitutes or who were simply promiscuous and behaving 'like a prostitute' lacked credibility as complainants, which made it difficult for the prosecution to prove the sexual assault beyond a reasonable doubt. Women in any of these categories were seen at law as 'commonly available' to men, as always consenting to sexual activity and thus, as not able to be raped. Men accused of sexual assault were therefore able to use evidence of prostitution to defend themselves, to undermine the credibility of rape complainants and to successfully avoid conviction.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Australian+and+New+Zealand+Journal+of+Criminology&amp;rft.atitle=Rape%2C+Prostitution+and+Consent&amp;rft.volume=40&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=127-142&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1375%2Facri.40.2.127&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A145263451%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.au=Sullivan%2C+Barbara&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexism"></span></span>
</li>
